## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly a time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics where reaction mechanisms are represented as rate laws dA_dt = f(A,t). With only {t, A} available, the most common relationships are reaction-order rate laws, reversible relaxation toward equilibrium, and time-varying effective rate constants (e.g., deactivation or changing operating conditions).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate depletion when the reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or second-order in A)
- n-th order power-law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical/global kinetics with apparent reaction order)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to a nonzero equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-form kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating production with depletion/saturation at high A)
- Chain-branching / polynomial rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competition between linear termination and quadratic branching in A)
- Rational inhibition (self-inhibition/crowding): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate rises with A but is inhibited at high A)
- Time-dependent deactivation (effective k decays): dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (catalyst deactivation or loss of activity over time)
- Time-dependent acceleration (warm-up/activation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) (rate constant ramps up from 0 to a plateau)
- Diffusion/mixing-limited effective rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (t + c1)**c2 (apparent rate slows with time due to transport limitations)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (externally driven periodic rate constant)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line in dA_dt vs A at fixed t), it indicates pseudo-first-order kinetics with an approximately constant rate coefficient.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 (linear in dA_dt vs A**2), it suggests bimolecular or second-order dependence in A.
- A nonzero steady state A* where dA_dt = 0 and the sign flips around A* implies reversible reaction or relaxation toward equilibrium (forms like -(A-c)).
- Concave-down depletion where the magnitude of dA_dt decreases faster than linearly as A falls is consistent with higher-than-first reaction order (A**n with n>1).
- A growth-then-decay pattern in dA_dt as A changes can indicate autocatalysis (A*(c-A)) where reaction accelerates at intermediate A but shuts down near 0 or saturation.
- A rate that depends on t even at the same A (scatter in dA_dt vs A across times) points to time-varying effective parameters, commonly modeled as k(t) multiplying A**n.
- Monotonic slowing with time at fixed A is often consistent with catalyst deactivation or poisoning, captured by multiplicative exp(-c*t) factors on the rate.
- An apparent singular/very-fast early-time rate that relaxes as t increases can indicate mixing or diffusion control, often modeled by division by (t+c)**p.
- Oscillatory components in time (sign-changing residuals vs t) suggest periodic forcing of the rate coefficient (sin/cos modulation).

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_w*cos(log(A + c4))
Candidate formulas: 83

GT (fixed):
\[
f(A)= -0.7725880991\,A^2\;-\;0.7725880991\,A\;+\;0.7402077580\;\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
Key structural requirements:
1) polynomial part is exactly a quadratic + linear with **no denominators**;  
2) oscillatory part is **cos(log(A+1))** (logarithm of affine in \(A\)), not sin of exp, not sin of log unless we can convert;  
3) no \(t\)-dependence.

Below, I check whether each candidate can be parameter-set to exactly this function (possibly assuming \(A\ge 0\) for Abs).

---

### Candidates 1–20 (all are rational-in-\(A\) with sin(exp(...)) pieces)
All of 1–20 have the general form “(polynomial in \(A\) and/or sin(exp(linear*A))) divided by (linear in \(A\))”, i.e. terms like \(\frac{A^2 c}{A c+1}\), \(\frac{A c}{A c+1}\), etc., and their trig parts are \(\sin(c\exp(cA)+c)\), not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\).

- You can remove the denominators only by setting the denominator coefficient to 0 (e.g. \(c1=0\Rightarrow A*c1+1=1\)), which turns those rational terms into plain polynomials.  
  However, even then the trig argument remains \(\exp(\text{linear }A)\), which cannot be made identically \(\log(A+1)\) for all \(A\) by choosing constants.
- You can also zero out the trig terms, but then you lose the required \(\cos(\log(A+1))\) component.

Therefore **none of 1–20** can match GT.

(Notes on specific outliers: 16 has a plain \(\sin(Ac+c)\) term—still not \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). 13 has a constant-over-linear term \(c7/(A c1+1)\) which cannot become the needed cosine term.)

---

### 21
\[
A^2c0 + A c1 + A c2 + \frac{A c3 e^{c4 t}}{A c5+1} + c6\sin(c7\log(A c8+1)+c9)
\]
Has explicit \(t\)-dependence unless \(c3=0\) or \(c4=0\) and still leaves a rational term; can set \(c3=0\) to remove it. Then we have polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\).  
But GT needs \(\cos(\log(A+1))\), which *could* be obtained from sine by phase shift: \(\sin(x+\pi/2)=\cos(x)\). So trig type is fine.

Problem: polynomial part here is \(A^2c0 + A(c1+c2)\) (no standalone \(-0.7726A\) issue—can set \(c0=-0.7726\) and \(c1+c2=-0.7726\)). Trig argument is \(\log(A c8+1)\): can set \(c8=1\). Trig amplitude \(c6\) can be \(0.740207758\). Phase \(c9\) can be \(\pi/2\). Frequency \(c7\) must be 1.

So **21 actually can match** provided we also eliminate the rational \(t\)-term by setting \(c3=0\). Then:
- \(c0=-0.7725880991\)
- \(c1+c2=-0.7725880991\) (choose any split)
- \(c6=0.7402077580\)
- \(c7=1\)
- \(c8=1\)
- \(c9=\pi/2\)
- \(c3=0\) (kills the \(t\)-dependent fraction)

This yields exactly:
\[
-0.7726A^2-0.7726A+0.7402\cos(\log(A+1)).
\]
So candidate 21 is a match.

---

### 22
Has \(\log(c5\exp(Ac6)+1)\) over \((Ac1+1)\). Even if denominator removed, argument is \(\log(1+c5 e^{Ac6})\), not \(\log(A+1)\). No way to make \(\log(1+c5 e^{Ac6})\equiv \log(A+1)\) for all \(A\). Not a match.

### 23
Has two different sine structures, one \(\sin(Ac+c)\) and one \(\sin(c + c\exp(Ac))\), both over \((Ac1+1)\). Cannot become \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). Not a match.

### 24
Same rational + sin(exp(...)) plus constant \(c9\). Cannot produce \(\cos(\log(A+1))\). Not a match.

### 25
Has \(\sin(Ac+c)\) and rational terms; no \(\log(A+1)\) inside trig. Not a match.

### 26–28
All are rational forms with \(\sin(\exp(\cdot))\) divided by \((Ac1+1)\). Not a match.

### 29
\[
A^2c0 + A c1 + A c2 + A c3 + c4 + c5\sin(c6\log(Ac7+1)+c8)
\]
This is polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) with no \(t\). This can match GT by phase shift and parameter choice:
- Set \(c0=-0.7725880991\)
- Set \(c1+c2+c3=-0.7725880991\)
- Set \(c4=0\) (GT has no constant offset)
- Trig: set \(c5=0.7402077580\), \(c6=1\), \(c7=1\), \(c8=\pi/2\) to convert sine to cosine.
So 29 can match as well.

### 30
Has \(A c0 + \sin(\log(\cdot)) + \log(\cdot)\) term. GT has no standalone log term; can set that coefficient \(c5=0\). But then no \(A^2\) term exists, so cannot match. Not a match.

### 31–35
31 has \(A c3 e^{c4 t}\) (remove with \(c3=0\)), leaving \(A^2\) + linear + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\): same as 29, so it can match.
32–34 similarly include \(t\)-dependent exponentials/powers; can be removed by setting their coefficients to 0, leaving polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\), hence can match.
35 is rational with \(\sin(\exp(\cdot))\) and a \(1/A\) term; cannot match.

### 36–43
36: \(A^2c0 + A c1 + c2\sin(c3\log(Ac4+1)+c5)\). This can match exactly (choose \(c0, c1\) as GT, and sine→cos via phase shift; set \(c3=1,c4=1,c2=0.7402,c5=\pi/2\)). So match.
37 includes an extra fixed \(+A\) term; could absorb into \(A c1\) by setting \(c1\) accordingly (since \(A c1 + A = A(c1+1)\)). So also match.
38,41,42,48 similarly are polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) (+ optional constants) and can be tuned (set constant offsets to 0). So match.
39 has two independent \(A^2\) terms but they just combine; still matchable.
40 has \(c5*Abs(A)^2\) plus linear term; lacks an explicit \(A^2\) unless you use Abs(A)^2 as \(A^2\) (works for all real A anyway). But it still lacks the separate \(-0.7726A^2\) unless you set \(c5=-0.7726\) and set linear \(A c0=-0.7726A\). Then trig is \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) convertible to cos. So match.
43 has an extra \(c7 e^{c8 t}\log(Ac9+1)\) term; can remove by setting \(c7=0\). Then match.

### 44–83
Most remaining candidates either:
- use \(\sin(Ac+c)\) (not \(\log(A+1)\)),
- use \(\exp(Ac)\) directly,
- use rational-in-\(A\) denominators that can be removed but still have wrong trig argument (\(\sin(\exp(\cdot))\), \(\sin(\log(\log(\cdot)))\), etc.),
- or include unavoidable extra \(t\)-terms unless coefficients are set to 0 (often removable).

Notably:
- 45 has \(\log(c6\exp(Ac7)+1)\) (wrong argument type), not match.
- 46 includes an extra \(c3\log(Ac4+1)\) term; can set \(c3=0\), then match (since it has \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\)).
- 50 includes \(c3\exp(Ac4)\); set \(c3=0\), then match.
- 53 includes an extra \(\sin(Ac+c)\); set its coefficient to 0, then match via the \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\) term.
- 55 has only sines (one log-sine and one linear-sine); can set linear-sine coefficient 0, but still lacks \(A^2\) term, so not match.
- 56,57 include extra rational/power terms; can set their coefficients to 0, then match.
- 60,62,63,64,67,71,73,79 include extra \(t\)-dependent terms; set their coefficients to 0, leaving matchable polynomial + \(\sin(\log(\cdot))\).
- 82: \(A c0 + A c1/(Ac2+1) + c3\sin(c4\log(Ac5+1)+c6)\). Even if you remove the rational term by setting \(c1=0\), you still lack an \(A^2\) term. Not match.
- 83 similarly lacks \(A^2\). Not match.
